**ββ) The connection-structures of the geometrical and the arithmetical: συνεχές and ἐφεξής.** εἰ ἔστι στιγμὴ καὶ μονάς, οὐχ οἷόν τε εἶναι μονάδα καὶ στιγμὴν τὸ αὐτό· ταῖς μὲν γὰρ ὑπάρχει τὸ ἅπτεσθαι, ταῖς δὲ μονάσιν τὸ ἐφεξής, καὶ τῶν μὲν ἐνδέχεται εἶναί τι μεταξύ (πᾶσα γὰρ γραμμὴ μεταξὺ στιγμῶν), τῶν δ' οὐκ ἀνάγκη· οὐδὲν γὰρ μεταξὺ δυάδος καὶ μονάδος (a27). To the points belongs ἅπτεσθαι, touching — indeed ἐχόμενον in the distinguished sense of συνεχές; to the μονάδες belongs only ἐφεξής. The connection-mode of the geometrical, the point, is characterized by συνεχές; the row of numbers by ἐφεξής, where *no touching* is necessary. Between two points there is always a stretch, more or less large; but between unit and two-ness there is *nothing*. So the being-together of the basic elements in the geometrical has the character of ἅπτεσθαι / συνεχές, that of the numbers the character of ἐφεξής, of *succession*. In regarding geometrical formations I must therefore posit something whose structure *co-posits more elements* than the ἐφεξής: the elements constitutive for the συνεχές are μέγεθος, πρός τι, θέσις, τόπος, ἅμα, ὑπομένον. The ὑπομένον, "being-there beforehand and remaining," belongs to what is determined by θέσις. *Therefore the geometrical is not so originary as the arithmetical.*

Heidegger draws out the ontological weight. For Aristotle the primary determination of *number*, insofar as it goes back to the μονάς as ἀρχή, has a still far more originary connection with the *constitution of the being itself*, since to the being-determination of *every* being belongs equally that it "is" and that it is "one": every ὄν is an ἕν. Thereby the ἀριθμός in the widest sense — the ἀριθμός standing here for the ἕν — gets, for the structure of beings *as such*, a more fundamental ontological significance; and it enters a connection with *λόγος*, insofar as the being in its last determinations becomes accessible only in a distinguished λόγος, in *νόησις*, while the geometrical structures are seen *in αἴσθησις alone*. αἴσθησις is where geometrical regarding must *halt*, στήσεται, has a *stand*; in arithmetic, by contrast, the λόγος, the νοεῖν, is at work, *disregarding* every θέσις, every intuitive dimension and orientation. This is why arithmetic is ἀκριβεστέρα: it operates *further from the perceptual*, in pure νοεῖν.

(Heidegger adds a contemporary aside: the question of the continuum has been rolled up again in present-day mathematics, and one comes back to Aristotelian thoughts insofar as one learns to understand that the continuum is *not analytically resolvable* but must be understood as something *pre-given*, prior to the question of an analytic penetration — work done by Hermann Weyl and made fruitful for mathematical physics, reached in connection with relativity theory, for which, against the "distance-geometry" of Newton's approach, the *field-concept* is decisive: physical being is determined by the field. He voices the hope that physicists may with time come, with philosophy's help, to appreciate more radically what Aristotle understood by movement, and to give up the prejudice that the Aristotelian concept of movement is primitive and that movement must be defined merely by velocity, which is only *one* character of movement.)

**γγ) Consequences for the taking-together of the manifold in geometry and arithmetic (*Cat.* 6).** *(Heidegger's Hs. gives only the citation; the interpretation to p.121 is reconstructed from Jonas/Schalk/Weiß.)* Aristotle holds the *Categories* genuine — "such a thing no pupil makes." τοῦ δὲ ποσοῦ τὸ μὲν ἐστι διωρισμένον, τὸ δὲ συνεχές· καὶ τὸ μὲν ἐκ θέσιν ἐχόντων πρὸς ἄλληλα τῶν ἐν αὐτοῖς μορίων συνέστηκε, τὸ δὲ οὐκ ἐξ ἐχόντων θέσιν (4b20). The *how-much* is divided into the συνεχές, the self-holding-together, and the διωρισμένον, the *in-itself-delimited*, where each moment of the manifold is bounded off against the other. The parts of the συνεχές relate to one another insofar as they are θέσιν ἔχοντα — and what is posited in this θέσις is *nothing other than the continuum itself*; this basic phenomenon is the *ontological condition* for there being such a thing as extension, μέγεθος: position and orientation are such that from one point to another one can continuously *proceed* — only so is movement intelligible. To the διωρισμένον belong ἀριθμός and λόγος; to the συνεχές, line, surface, body, and further χρόνος and τόπος.

How are units of the *number-row* taken together? τῶν μὲν γὰρ τοῦ ἀριθμοῦ μορίων οὐδείς ἐστι κοινὸς ὅρος, πρὸς ὃν συνάπτει τὰ μόρια αὐτοῦ (4b25). The parts of a number have *no common ὅρος*, no common boundary such that through the ὅρος (here identical with the καθόλου) each part would be *evenly determined*. Take 10: for the two μόρια, 5 and 5, there is no κοινὸς ὅρος; each is for itself, διωρισμένον; each is something other. 7 + 3 is 10, but 7 has no relation in the sense of the καθόλου or κοινόν to 10 or 3. The peculiar relation holds that the μόρια *cannot be taken together*, συνάπτεσθαι: οὐδ' ὅλως ἂν ἔχοις ἐπ' ἀριθμοῦ λαβεῖν κοινὸν ὅρον τῶν μορίων, ἀλλ' ἀεὶ διώρισται (4b29). There is *no* κοινόν for the manifold of numbers with reference to which each single number would be a *case*, so that number would be the καθόλου — no *generalization*, no *genus "number"* for the single numbers. A negative result, but a pressing-through to the peculiar connection lying in the number-row.

The same at λόγος: ὡσαύτως δὲ καὶ ὁ λόγος τῶν διωρισμένων ἐστίν (4b32). λόγος here is seen as a μετὰ φωνῆς γιγνόμενος, a *vocalization*, articulated into single syllables as its στοιχεῖα; measured out by long and short syllable, it is a ποσόν whose single parts are *absolutely bounded off* against one another. Every syllable is autonomous; there is *no syllable-in-general* representing the common of all syllables — whereas there *is* a point that is like all points. (The λόγος-example is a favorite of Aristotle and Plato for the question of the peculiar *unity of a manifold* that is not continuously composed but whose every part is autonomous.) So the line has *another* mode of unity: ἡ δὲ γραμμὴ συνεχές ἐστιν· ἔστι γὰρ λαβεῖν κοινὸν ὅρον πρὸς ὃν τὰ μόρια αὐτῆς συνάπτει, στιγμήν· καὶ τῆς ἐπιφανείας γραμμήν (5a1). From the line one *can* take out something to which each part of the line can be addressed in the same sense — a point — though these taken-out points do *not* in composition *make up* the line. The remarkable ground of possibility of this κοινὸς ὅρος is that the line *is more than a manifold of points*: it has a *θέσις*. The number-row lacks θέσις, is determined only by ἐφεξής; and insofar as grasping the bare succession does *not* require the co-positing of a θέσις, it is, seen *from grasping as such, from νοεῖν*, the simpler and more originary — the ontological reason arithmetic outranks geometry in strictness.

The whole excursus thus arms the Plato-interpretation at three points: it fixes χωρίζειν as the legitimate act of mathematical abstraction and marks the exact spot where Plato *illegitimately* extends it to the ἀρχαί of the moved world (leaving out κίνησις and τόπος); it exhibits τόπος as a *δύναμις* co-constituting a being's presence, so that "being at a place" is an ontological, not a spatial-geometric, determination; and it grounds the ranking of arithmetic over geometry in the difference between νοεῖν (which disregards θέσις) and αἴσθησις (at which geometry must halt) — the same difference between λόγος and αἴσθησις that has governed the account of σοφία throughout.

Heidegger closes the excursus by drawing the ontological lesson for the Plato-interpretation. Seen from *grasping as such, from νοεῖν*, number is *ontologically earlier*: it characterizes a being still *free* from orientation toward the being that has the character of *continuum* and is ultimately an αἰσθητόν. Therefore number comes into an originary connection when one asks after the *structure of the being as the "something."* Herein is grounded that *Plato's radical ontological reflection sets in at number*: number is more originary, and every determination of the being along the guiding thread of number in the widest sense is *more in the nearness of the last ἀρχαί of the ὄν*. When Aristotle adduces the difference of geometry and arithmetic (*Met.* I, 2), his sole concern is to show that within the ἐπιστῆμαι there is a *gradation of strictness* — not to claim arithmetic is the most originary science of the being in its being. On the contrary, Aristotle shows precisely that the proper ἀρχή of number, the unit, is *itself no longer number* — whereby a still more originary discipline is pre-sketched, one that studies the *basic constitution of the being*: σοφία.

#### §16. Continuation: σοφία (*Met.* I, 2; Part 1). The fourth essential moment of σοφία: the autonomy of ἀληθεύειν (ἑαυτῆς ἕνεκεν, μὴ πρὸς χρῆσιν)

The fourth and last moment is that σοφία *is in itself autonomous*. Aristotle shows this in two ways: from the *theme* of σοφία, and from the *comportment of Dasein itself*.

##### a) The theme of σοφία. The ἀγαθόν as τέλος and last οὗ ἕνεκα; as αἴτιον and ἀρχή; as object of pure θεωρεῖν

τὸ δ' εἰδέναι καὶ τὸ ἐπίστασθαι αὐτῶν ἕνεκα μάλισθ' ὑπάρχει τῇ τοῦ μάλιστ' ἐπιστητοῦ ἐπιστήμῃ (982a30): the seeing and knowing *for their own sake* lie most in that ἐπιστήμη whose theme is the *μάλιστα ἐπιστητόν*, the most-knowable. This most-knowable — what most shapes knowing into a proper knowing — is what is grasped when it comes to winning, within the being, the *last orientations*, to seeing *for the sake of which* this or that should happen. This last for-the-sake-of-which, οὗ ἕνεκα, is *as τέλος always an ἀγαθόν* (*Met.* I, 3; 983a31). But the ἀγαθόν is the affair of the *ἀρχικωτάτη* among the ἐπιστῆμαι and τέχναι — the most governing being the one that γνωρίζουσα τίνος ἕνεκέν ἐστι πρακτέον ἕκαστον (982b5), gives information about *for the sake of which* each single thing is to be brought about. Accordingly σοφία, insofar as it is μάλιστα ἐπιστήμη and as such gives information about the μάλιστα ἀγαθόν, the ὅλως τὸ ἄριστον ἐν τῇ φύσει πάσῃ (982b7), is the *ἀρχικωτάτη* among all ἐπιστῆμαι and τέχναι whatever — the one no longer *led* but that, expressly or unexpressly, *has the lead* and so is *autonomous*. In σοφία lies enclosed the question which is the ἄριστον, from which the orientation for every further τέχνη and ἐπιστήμη is to be won.

But this characterization — that σοφία *aims at an ἀγαθόν* — brings Aristotle into *dangerous nearness* to another relation to the being: to *πρᾶξις*, which remains oriented precisely to the for-the-sake-of-which. If σοφία aims at the ἀγαθόν, it looks as though it were ultimately a πρᾶξις, whereas it was just shown that, *freed from χρῆσις*, it is a *pure θεωρεῖν*. The difficulty: here is a Dasein-comportment that (1) relates to a being determined *as ἀγαθόν* and yet (2) is to be *no πρᾶξις* but a *θεωρεῖν*.

The resolution lies in Aristotle's stress that *the ἀγαθόν too is one of the causes*, καὶ γὰρ τἀγαθὸν ἓν τῶν αἰτίων ἐστίν (982b10). The basic character of the αἴτιον is to be *ἀρχή*, the last from which I understand something: μάλιστα δ' ἐπιστητὰ τὰ πρῶτα καὶ τὰ αἴτια (982b2). The important thing is not merely that Aristotle says the ἀγαθόν is an αἴτιον, but that he succeeded, *for the first time*, in showing that the ἀγαθόν is *nothing other than a being-determination of the being that is determined by the τέλος*. Insofar as a being has become *finished* in its τέλος, it is as it *ought* to be. The ἀγαθόν has at first *no reference to πρᾶξις at all*, but is a determination of the being insofar as it is *finished, complete*. What *always is* need not first be produced; it is always already *standingly finished there*. Insofar as Aristotle understands the ἀγαθόν as τέλος — being-finished — and reckons the τέλος in among the other causes (ὕλη, εἶδος, ἀρχὴ κινήσεως), he wins for the first time an *ontological basic-understanding of the ἀγαθόν*. To grasp the ἀγαθόν as a "value" is a *counter-sense*. Its proper sense is rather:

ἀγαθόν → τέλος → πέρας → ἀρχὴ τοῦ ὄντος.

This proper sense must be held fast if the expression ἀγαθόν is to be understood as a properly *philosophical* term. Thereby the situation changes: insofar as the ἀγαθόν is understood *not* primarily as related to πρᾶξις but as the *basic constitution of the being at itself*, the possibility is pre-sketched that the ἀγαθόν *as ἀρχή* is precisely the object of a *θεωρεῖν* — indeed that with respect to this being *as ἀεὶ ὄν*, as always-being (with respect to which I *cannot act*), the *right* relation is *θεωρία*. This possibility is pre-sketched by the interpretation of the ἀγαθόν as *πέρας*. So, although the ἀγαθόν is oriented to πρᾶξις, on the ground of the ontological basic-understanding of the ἀγαθόν the way stays *free* for a comportment that, *as theoretical*, is the right comportment to the ἀγαθόν. Hence Aristotle can say σοφία, in which he sees this θεωρεῖν, is a quite peculiar φρόνησις, a *τοιαύτη φρόνησις* (982b24) — not φρόνησις as we know it, related to the being that can be otherwise, the being of action, but a φρόνησις that goes to an ἀγαθόν which is *not πρακτόν*. That Aristotle here calls σοφία a *τοιαύτη φρόνησις* at once indicates an *orientation against Plato*, who did not come clear in distinguishing the phenomena: in calling σοφία a φρόνησις, Aristotle indicates that he sees in σοφία — as Plato saw in φρόνησις — the *highest kind of ἀληθεύειν* and the highest comportment, the highest existence-possibility of the human.

So far we know from the γένεσις of σοφία that it *more and more disregards* practical purposing. But that σοφία is μὴ πρὸς χρῆσιν is a determination given only *negatively* and *in passing*, with regard to other things; it does not yet determine σοφία itself. It must now be shown *positively* that σοφία is *pre-sketched in Dasein itself* according to its possibility — that it is the *cultivation of a primary being-possibility of Dasein itself*. Only thereby does the autonomy of σοφία become ontologically intelligible, and the discussion regarding φρόνησις is brought onto the right ground: the possibility is to be shown that φρόνησις (1) *no longer* has ζωή *as πρακτόν* for its theme, yet (2) *as ἀληθεύειν* is *a being-mode of ζωή*.

##### b) The origin of σοφία out of Dasein itself. θαυμάζειν and ἀπορεῖν as the origin of philosophy. The tendency toward pure θεωρεῖν lying in Dasein itself

Already in primitive and everyday Dasein lies the *root* of the autonomous mere-regarding of the world. Aristotle shows that σοφία's *not* going to ποίησις and πρᾶξις is not accidental and after-the-fact but so *from the beginning and originarily*: ὅτι δ' οὐ ποιητική, δῆλον καὶ ἐκ τῶν πρώτων φιλοσοφησάντων. διὰ γὰρ τὸ θαυμάζειν οἱ ἄνθρωποι καὶ νῦν καὶ τὸ πρῶτον ἤρξαντο φιλοσοφεῖν (982b11). That σοφία from the outset makes up, *beside ποίησις*, an autonomous being-mode of Dasein becomes visible from two primary enactment-moments of Dasein: *θαυμάζειν* (wondering) and *διαπορεῖν* (working-through the impasse).

(1) σοφία takes its departure from *θαυμάζεσθαι*, reached early in natural Dasein. θαυμάζει εἰ οὕτως ἔχει (983a13): one wonders at something that meets one, *whether it really stands so* as it shows itself. θαυμαστὸν γὰρ εἶναι δοκεῖ πᾶσιν, εἴ τι τῷ ἐλαχίστῳ μὴ μετρεῖται (983a16): wondrous for all is when something is *not* to be measured by the smallest — fundamentally, when something is not to be made intelligible by the *most familiar* one disposes over. μετρεῖν, to measure, determine, is the way Dasein makes something intelligible to itself; μέτρον, ἀριθμός belong in the same domain as λόγος, that of *ἀληθεύειν*. The θαυμαστόν is *what does not fit* — "here something does not add up." Something is wondrous for a regarding insofar as this, with the understanding it disposes over, *does not get through* at the encountered fact; it *strikes against* what shows itself. The wondering began at first only at what *lies to hand*, τὰ πρόχειρα (982b13); later regard went gradually further, wondering at greater things at first taken as self-evident — the παθήματα of the moon, that the moon *changes*, what happens with the sun, and finally at the *coming-to-be of the being as a whole*, that it is there as it shows itself.

(2) This self-wondering as originary phenomenon of Dasein Aristotle interprets so as to show a *tendency toward a θεωρεῖν* asserting itself in it: in Dasein there is *from the outset* a tendency toward *mere-seeing-and-merely-understanding*. Here Aristotle uses an expression current in the philosophy of the day: *ἀπορεῖν*. ἄπορος is what is *without passage*, where one does not get through; πόρος originally means the passage through a river at a shallow place; ἀπορία: the regarding of the world *does not get through*, finds no way. With the at-first-known αἴτια, the available means of explanation, one does not get through; the way of explanatory running-through is *barred*; how the matter properly looks is, as it at first shows itself, *distorted*. Here ἀπορία corresponds wholly to the sense of ἀληθεύειν and the conception of Dasein already met: the being of the world is at first *closed off*, and Dasein does not get through. In this sense of ἀληθεύειν, whose nearest enactment-form is λόγος, the correspondences hold: ἀπορεῖν / ἀπορία / ἀπορούμενον answer to λέγειν / λόγος / λεγόμενον.

This ἀπορεῖν, expressly enacted, points to one's *not knowing* the matter one does not get through: ὁ δ' ἀπορῶν οἴεται ἀγνοεῖν (982b17). The one who does not get through and finds no exit, and *establishes* that the matter is closed to him, is convinced he is *not yet properly familiar* with it, does not yet know it. Insofar as, precisely in this conviction, he becomes *transparent to himself* in the not-getting-through, continuing the *διαπορεῖν* and making attempts to press through, there lies in such ἀπορεῖν and διαπορεῖν a *φεύγειν τὴν ἄγνοιαν* (fleeing ignorance) and a *διώκειν τὸ ἐπίστασθαι* (pursuing knowing): ὥστ' εἴπερ διὰ τὸ φεύγειν τὴν ἄγνοιαν ἐφιλοσόφησαν, φανερὸν ὅτι διὰ τὸ εἰδέναι τὸ ἐπίστασθαι ἐδίωκον καὶ οὐ χρήσεώς τινος ἕνεκεν (982b19). Whoever continues the διαπορεῖν betrays in the effort that he *flees ignorance*, the concealed, and *pursues* the ἐπίστασθαι, the having-uncovered of the being. So ἀπορία marks the peculiar *passage-station* of Dasein over against the world — a peculiar *being-underway*: in a way to *know* about the being, and yet *not to get through*. ἀπορεῖν has in itself no autonomous, positive sense, but only the *functional* sense of the right *pursuit* of the knowing of the being itself. δια-πορεῖν, the pressing-forward interrogating, means: no longer to find something *self-evident* — where "self-evident" is what is understood out of the understanding one just happens to have — but to seek to *win the matter's understanding from the matter itself*. The positive steps in διαπορεῖν are nothing but the *making-present of the determinate matter*. Way and direction of ἀπορεῖν go *from the environing-world to the world*, such that ἀπορεῖν goes not to what merely accidentally meets one and just strikes one, but includes that *Dasein sets itself on the way*, whereby what strikes it is *what is always already there*. Where such ἀπορεῖν is, there is this *setting-oneself-on-the-way*, the being-underway-toward. So ἀπορεῖν/διαπορεῖν becomes, in both natural regarding and express scientific research, the phenomenon showing how far Dasein *in itself* aims at the uncovering of the being *solely for the sake of the uncovering itself*. With this the last determination of σοφία is won, and at once it is seen that *θεωρεῖν is a wholly autonomous comportment of Dasein, related to nothing else*.

#### §17. Summary: the modes of ἀληθεύειν as modifications of self-orienting Dasein

We have won an insight into Dasein insofar as various modes of ἀληθεύειν at first lie in it *not delimited against one another*, so that a *multivocity* holds regarding the use of the expressions τέχνη, ἐπιστήμη, φρόνησις, σοφία. The formation of this multivocity is *not arbitrary*, and its real overcoming cannot happen by holding *dogmatic definitions* against it and fixing these comportments. The multivocity is overcome only when its *motives* become visible — when it becomes intelligible *why* these different expressions are used in this multivocity.

Dasein uncovers its nearest environing-world; it *orients itself* in its world without the single modes of self-orienting being made express. Insofar as this self-orienting is a taking-cognizance and deliberating *directed to producing*, it is of the kind of *τέχνη*. Insofar as this knowing-one's-way is still a *knowing* and expressly steps forth *as* knowing, the same fact can be grasped as *ἐπιστήμη* — which need not yet be science at all. Insofar as the self-orienting goes to a *πρακτόν* handled for one's *own use* (αὑτῷ, for oneself), this self-orienting is *φρόνησις* in the widest sense, as it belongs to the ζῷα — whether what is discovered is the ποιητόν of a πρᾶξις or not makes no difference here. Insofar as the self-orienting goes *expressly to the αἴτιον* and becomes merely a *real understanding*, the same modes of self-orienting — τέχνη, ἐπιστήμη, φρόνησις — can also be grasped as *σοφία*. This is the fundamental use of these expressions in Dasein itself, and one must make it fundamentally clear in order to see that the *γένεσις* to express Dasein-modes is enacted *out of Dasein itself*.

It has shown itself that Dasein aims at σοφία *only διὰ τὸ εἰδέναι* and *not χρήσεώς τινος ἕνεκεν* (982b20), that θεωρεῖν is a wholly autonomous comportment related to nothing else. So σοφία reveals a possibility of Dasein in which Dasein betrays itself as *free*, as wholly *set upon itself*: ὥσπερ ἄνθρωπός φαμεν ἐλεύθερος ὁ ἑαυτοῦ ἕνεκα καὶ μὴ ἄλλου ὤν, οὕτω καὶ αὐτὴ μόνη ἐλευθέρα οὖσα τῶν ἐπιστημῶν· μόνη γὰρ αὐτὴ ἑαυτῆς ἕνεκέν ἐστιν (982b25) — as we call that human *free* who is for his own sake and not another's, so σοφία *alone* among the sciences is free, for it alone is *for its own sake*. And so the question arises whether such a Dasein-possibility is *at all graspable* for human Dasein, since the ζωή of the human is *δούλη* (982b29), the life of the human, its being-in-the-world, in a way *servant* of the circumstances, of the urgencies of the everyday. It seems, insofar as human Dasein is a servant, that the possibility of the autonomous comportment in pure θεωρία must remain *denied* it — that σοφία can be no possible *κτῆσις* (possession) for the human. The question thus stands whether σοφία can be *κτῆσις ἀνθρώπου* — the same question the *Nicomachean Ethics* poses as whether σοφία can be a possible *ἕξις* of human Dasein.

Only after clarifying this will we be sufficiently prepared for the decision whether *φρόνησις*, which as such has *human Dasein itself* for the goal of its uncovering, or whether *σοφία* is the *highest* kind of uncovering. We will have to see from where Aristotle makes the decision about the being-mode of φρόνησις over against the being-mode of σοφία as a possibility of human Dasein. From this determination it becomes at once intelligible in what sense there can be, regarding human life, such a thing as a *science* like *ethics* — insofar as ethics occupies itself with the ἦθος, the being of the human, which *can also be otherwise*. It is asked how far there can be a science of such a thing, if indeed proper science goes to a being that *always is*. This is the aporia — a science of the changeable — that hands the course forward from the *Nicomachean Ethics* VI framework into the confrontation of σοφία and φρόνησις that will decide the ranking, and with it the meaning of the philosophical existence the *Sophist* depicts.

### Third Chapter: The question of the priority of φρόνησις or σοφία as the highest modes of ἀληθεύειν (*Met.* I, 2, Part 2; *Nic. Eth.* VI, 7–10; X, 6–7)

#### §18. The divinity of σοφία and the questionableness of σοφία as a possibility of the human (*Met.* I, 2, Part 2). σοφία as constant being-alongside the ἀεί. Human Dasein as "servant" (δούλη) of the ἀναγκαῖα and the ἄλλως ἔχοντα. The priority of σοφία with respect to ἀληθεύειν

The question is whether σοφία can be *κτῆσις* and *ἕξις* of the human. Aristotle first poses it by citing Greek poetry — Simonides' line that only a god may have this prerogative (982b31) — which says σοφία is a *θεῖον*. Here, in *Met.* I, 2, it is at first only *natural Dasein* that speaks: that the θεός alone has the possibility of the καθ' αὑτόν ἐπιστήμη (982b31), i.e. σοφία, reserved to the gods. What other possibility should the gods have? The poets add that the gods are *envious* of humans, begrudging them σοφία. But on such claims of the poets, Aristotle says, not much is to be given, since — as the proverb runs — "the poets lie much" (983a4). The gods cannot be envious at all, not because they are too good for it, but because *all πάθη, all affects, are excluded from the being of the θεῖον*. On the other hand there is no higher kind of knowing than σοφία. Aristotle shows this cautiously: σοφία might perhaps most of all be a god's actual possession, and therefore one may with right address it as a θεῖον; further because the *object* of σοφία is an always-being, θεῖον. He leaves the question standing. Note that Aristotle, in ascribing σοφία to the θεῖον, does not speak *absolutely*, not as a fact but as a *possibility*. He closes: ἀναγκαιότεραι μὲν οὖν πᾶσαι ταύτης, ἀμείνων δ' οὐδεμία (983a10) — all modes of knowing in the widest sense are *more necessary, more urgent* for Dasein than σοφία, but *none is better*. σοφία has, with respect to ἀληθεύειν, the uncovering of the being, the *priority*.

Over against this rather popular discussion Aristotle has a far more originary understanding of the questions raised, and treating the difficulties leads him to show that σοφία *is* the highest possibility for the human. σοφία is by its idea: τῶν ἐξ ἀρχῆς αἰτίων ἐπιστήμη (*Met.* I, 3; 983a24), the science of the origin-causes. This idea demands — as regards the being of ἀληθεύειν, the being-mode of Dasein — (1) *complete autonomy in itself*, and (2) *the comportment to the properly-being in its being, the tarrying alongside this*. It demands the free being-set-upon-oneself in the *having-present of the being at itself*. And thus the question: can σοφία be κτῆσις and ἕξις of the human? For human Dasein is *δούλη*; it is *assigned to* the ἀναγκαῖα, which are ἄλλως ἔχοντα; it is *compelled* to being-alongside such ἀναγκαῖα and ἄλλως ἔχοντα. The human *cannot constantly be alongside the τιμιώτατα*; the constant being — the always-being in this autonomous being-mode alongside the τιμιώτατα — does not come into consideration for him.

The question sharpens when one refers to σοφία's being a *θεῖον*. When Aristotle characterizes σοφία as a θεῖον, this happens in *purely ontological* purposing; *metaphysics is not theology*. It is an ἐπιστήμη, σοφία, that is θειοτάτη — and this in two ways: (1) it is *κτῆσις of a θεός*; (2) it has for its theme *τὰ θεῖα*. This points far ahead into Aristotle's "Metaphysics." σοφία, insofar as (1) it is κτῆσις of a θεός, insofar as the comportment in it is a divine one, is *νοῦς, νοεῖν, νόησις*; insofar as (2) it is τῶν θείων, has for object the θεῖον, it is *νοήσεως*. So: σοφία (1) κτῆσις of a θεός — νόησις; (2) theme τὰ θεῖα — νοήσεως. [The νόησις νοήσεως of *Met.* XII stands in the background.] According to our investigations, the θεῖον presents itself in σοφία thus: σοφία, (1) insofar as it has the θεῖον for object, has for object the *ἀεί*; (2) insofar as the θεῖον is in it *as comportment*, it is a *mere regarding, a mere θεωρεῖν*. The comportment of σοφία is such that it is *adequate to its object*: it tarries *constantly* alongside the always-being; it is distinguished by *remaining constantly alongside* as θεωρεῖν. So the idea of this being of Dasein lies in its being *constantly present alongside the ἀεί*.

*However*, Aristotle stresses, human Dasein does *not endure* in this comportment the *whole time* of its life. The *kind of its being-temporal* makes it *impossible* to be constantly alongside the ἀεί. The human *needs recreation, relaxation*, from θεωρεῖν. These connections in a way underlie the *Met.* I, 2 consideration without his going into them expressly. But this much is clear: the *being-relation of Dasein to the ἀεί, if it is to be adequate, must be an ever-θεωρεῖν* — which is in a certain way possible, in a certain way not. With this the task of delimiting σοφία against φρόνησις is *not* settled, for φρόνησις raises *of itself* the claim to be the highest kind of knowing of the human.

#### §19. φρόνησις as the proper possibility of the human, and the rejection of φρόνησις as "σοφία" (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 7, Part 2). The seriousness of φρόνησις. The ἀκρότατον ἀγαθὸν ἀνθρώπινον as object of φρόνησις. The ἄριστον ἐν τῷ κόσμῳ as object of σοφία. Pre-sketch of ontological superiority as the criterion of σοφία's priority

φρόνησις raises of itself the claim to be the highest kind of knowing of the human, insofar as one can say it is the one to which *most seriousness* belongs, because with it it is a matter of *the Dasein of the human itself*; it is the σπουδαιοτάτη (1141a21). σοφία may treat of the τιμιώτατα, the highest being — but this being is what *does not concern* the human in his existence. What concerns the human is *Dasein itself*, the ἀκρότατον ἀγαθὸν ἀνθρώπινον, εὐδαιμονία. For this φρόνησις gives the way-pointing; it makes Dasein transparent in the carrying-out of such an action as brings the human to the *εὖ*. If then φρόνησις is the most earnest and decisive knowing, the science moving in φρόνησις' field will be the highest. Insofar as the human is not alone, insofar as humans are *with one another*, *πολιτική* (1141a21) is the highest science; accordingly πολιτικὴ ἐπιστήμη is the proper σοφία, and the πολιτικός the right *φιλόσοφος* — *this is Plato's conception*.

But it is questionable whether this determination of φρόνησις in relation to σοφία holds by right. Note what Aristotle brings into the field. The ἀγαθόν, as ἀγαθόν of the human's Dasein, as εὐδαιμονία, is indeed an ἀκρότατον ἀγαθόν, that in which the human's Dasein reaches its *completion*. But it is still an *ἀνθρώπινον* ἀγαθόν, a determination of the *being of the human*, and as such an *ἕτερον* (a23) over against the ἀγαθόν that is, e.g., the fish's. According to the being of the respective being, the ἀγαθόν as τέλος is in each case another; further, the ἀγαθόν can also be, for single humans in their Dasein-possibility, in each case another. Insofar as the ἀγαθόν can in each case be another, we have in the ἀγαθόν a being-determination of a being that *can also be otherwise* — *not ἀεί*. The Dasein of the human is not something that *wills to be ἀεί* — whereas the λευκόν or the εὐθύ is a τὸ αὐτὸ ἀεί (a24), "always identical"; such being-determinations always are what they are, and are therefore a *σοφόν*, object of σοφία. If one wants to say σοφία goes to such a being as is αὑτῷ ὠφέλιμον (advantageous to itself), then there would be *several σοφίαι* — one for humans, one for animals, etc.

The identification of φρόνησις and σοφία would be *in the right* only if the human were the *ἄριστον τῶν ἐν τῷ κόσμῳ* (a21), the "properly-being of what is in the world." The question whether φρόνησις itself is σοφία must be oriented *fundamentally at the being to which both go*, at the ἀκρότατον ἀγαθόν. εἰ δ' ὅτι βέλτιστον ἄνθρωπος τῶν ἄλλων ζῴων, οὐδὲν διαφέρει (a33): "that the human is the βέλτιστον over against the other living beings makes no difference." For there is *other, much more divine* being ἐν τῷ κόσμῳ than human Dasein: καὶ γὰρ ἀνθρώπου ἄλλα πολὺ θειότερα τὴν φύσιν (a34). There is still *θειότερα τὴν φύσιν* — φύσις here says as much as *οὐσία* — there is still other than human Dasein that, as regards the *kind of its being-present*, is *more properly present*. θεῖον here says merely *the higher kind of being of the being*. Of religion and god and a religiosity of Aristotle there is here *no talk at all*; θειότερον as expression for the higher kind of being has a *purely formal-ontological sense*. This is clear from what Aristotle adduces as evidence for the "more divine" being: φανερώτατα ἐξ ὧν ὁ κόσμος συνέστηκεν (b1), what is *most manifest, wholly uncovered* of that out of which the "world" consists — οὐρανός, ἥλιος, σελήνη. (The proof that Aristotle held the sun for a god would be hard to furnish.) ἐκ δὴ τῶν εἰρημένων δῆλον ὅτι ἡ σοφία ἐστὶν καὶ ἐπιστήμη καὶ νοῦς τῶν τιμιωτάτων τῇ φύσει (b2): σοφία is ἐπιστήμη and νοῦς of the *τιμιώτατα τῇ φύσει* — of what, as regards the kind of its being-present, has the *priority* and so is the properly-present. For Aristotle and the Greeks, as for the tradition, the properly-being is *what always is, what is constantly already there*. (The Greeks made this clear *to themselves*; today one merely *believes* it.) The Dasein of the human, if it is already an ἄριστον, is still not an ἄριστον *ἁπλῶς* or *φύσει*, but only an ἄριστον *πρὸς ἡμᾶς*. The Dasein of the human is *not ἀεί*, not always; the being of the human *comes to be and passes away*, it has its determinate *time, its αἰών*.

With this it is pre-sketched *where the basis for σοφία's preference over φρόνησις lies*. σοφία has the priority *in respect of the being at itself*, insofar as the being to which it goes has, Greek-ontologically, the priority. The being comes into view *out of what it, at itself, always already is*. Aristotle closes the exposition of σοφία (1141b3) with a renewed enumeration of the characters marking σoφία's autonomy and its self-standing genesis in Dasein. But the two modes of ἀληθεύειν, φρόνησις and σοφία, are distinguished *not only from the object but in their own structure*. To see this needs a closer regard of the structure of φρόνησις itself.

#### §20. More radical grasp of φρόνησις (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 8–9)

##### a) φρόνησις as πρακτικὴ ἕξις (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 8)

To see how far φρόνησις and σοφία differ *in their structure*: φρόνησις is an ἀληθεύειν, but one that *in itself* is referred to πρᾶξις. "In itself" means the πρᾶξις is not something that lies *beside*, that comes *after* — as the ἔργον does in τέχνη — but *every step* of φρόνησις' ἀληθεύειν is oriented to the πρακτόν. Accordingly the *mode of enactment* of ἀληθεύειν in φρόνησις is another than in σοφία. In *Nic. Eth.* VI, from ch. 8 on, Aristotle lays this out.

φρόνησις is a *πρακτικὴ ἕξις*, for what φρόνησις uncovers is the πρακτὸν ἀγαθόν (1141b12). Its specific ἕξις-character is *εὐβουλεύεσθαι*, deliberating-well: ὁ δ' ἁπλῶς εὔβουλος ὁ τοῦ ἀρίστου ἀνθρώπῳ τῶν πρακτῶν στοχαστικὸς κατὰ τὸν λογισμόν (1141b12). The one who deliberates simply-adequately — whose deliberation and circumspection *comes into the τέλος*, to the end and being-finished — is the one who uncovers the *ἄριστον ἀνθρώπῳ*, the best for the human, in what it is, and specifically the ἄριστον *τῶν πρακτῶν*, the best among the possible πρακτά. This is what grants the human εὐδαιμονία, which is the οὗ ἕνεκα for the human. Such uncovering the ἁπλῶς εὔβουλος can achieve because he is στοχαστικός, "can hit the mark," and κατὰ τὸν λογισμόν, "in deliberating and talking-through" human Dasein in its concrete being-possibilities.

But: οὐδ' ἔστιν ἡ φρόνησις τῶν καθόλου μόνον (1141b14). Such uncovering of the ἄριστον is *not* out solely to exhibit, as it were, the mere *look* of the nearest Dasein-kind of the human; there the task of φρόνησις would not only not come to an end but would be fundamentally *misunderstood*. φρόνησις' ἀληθεύειν as such δεῖ καὶ τὰ καθ' ἕκαστα γνωρίζειν (1141b15), "must also uncover the concrete single being-possibilities of Dasein," πρακτικὴ γάρ, ἡ δὲ πρᾶξις περὶ τὰ καθ' ἕκαστα (1141b16). Its uncovering is *ὁμολόγως ὀρέξει* — enacted in *constant regard to the situation of the acting one*, of a deciding now, here. From this the sense of the ἀγαθόν for human Dasein, and its treatment in λέγειν, is determined not incidentally but by its ownmost sense: it is an *ἀκρότατον*. φρόνησις is *not* ἕξις μετὰ λόγου μόνον (VI, 5; 1140b28), not a mere free-running through-speaking of something; already in *every word*, every dictum it makes, it speaks *of* the πρακτόν and *for* it. ἡ δὲ φρόνησις πρακτική· ὥστε δεῖ ἄμφω ἔχειν, ἢ ταύτην μᾶλλον (1141b21): φρόνησις must have *both* — the ἀληθεύειν and the πρᾶξις — "or rather this latter still more." φρόνησις is in the πρᾶξις still more than in the λόγος. The *decisive* thing in φρόνησις is the πρᾶξις: the πρᾶξις is in φρόνησις both ἀρχή and τέλος. In fore-regard to a determinate action φρόνησις is enacted, and it comes to its *end in the action itself*.

εἴη δ' ἄν τις καὶ ἐνταῦθα ἀρχιτεκτονική (1141b22): here too, within the πρακτική, there is a certain *order-nexus*, a leading and guidance. Insofar as the ἄνθρωπος is the ζῷον πολιτικόν, the πρᾶξις is to be understood as *being in being-with-one-another*; and insofar as this is τέλος, φρόνησις is of the kind of *πολιτική*. So the decisive thing for φρόνησις is the πρᾶξις — from which follows an essential difference between φρόνησις and ἐπιστήμη concerning their *genesis*, shown in ch. 9.

##### b) The mode of arising of φρόνησις and ἐπιστήμη (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 9). φρόνησις: ἐξ ἐμπειρίας (life-experience). Mathematics: δι' ἀφαιρέσεως

To φρόνησις belongs *χρόνος*. To the right possibility of decision belongs *life-experience* — but *not* to ἐπιστήμη. Hence it can happen that *young* humans are in a position to discover important things: Aristotle adduces the mathematician (Pascal would be an example), for mathematics is an autonomous *σχολάζειν*. γεωμετρικοὶ μὲν νέοι καὶ μαθηματικοὶ γίνονται καὶ σοφοὶ τὰ τοιαῦτα (1142a12): precisely in mathematics quite young humans can research independently and become σοφοί in this respect — for mathematics needs no γνῶσις of the καθ' ἕκαστα, which is won only through ἐμπειρία, life-experience. νέος δ' ἔμπειρος οὐκ ἔστιν (1142a15): young humans are *not broken-in* to the facts of human Dasein itself, πλῆθος γὰρ χρόνου ποιεῖ τὴν ἐμπειρίαν (1142a15) — only through *much time*, through the many nows of the "as-soon-as–then," is life-experience possible; it is reserved to the ripeness of age. So to φρόνησις too belongs πλῆθος χρόνου, "much time," because φρόνησις needs life-experience, being τῶν καθ' ἕκαστα (1142a14). φρόνησις is therefore not properly the affair of the young — whereas the young *can* be σοφοὶ τὰ τοιαῦτα, σοφοί with respect to mathematics.

Yet there is a difference between mathematical and philosophical knowing. Quite young people can have mathematical knowing, but *not* philosophical: ἢ ὅτι τὰ μὲν δι' ἀφαιρέσεώς ἐστιν, τῶν δ' αἱ ἀρχαὶ ἐξ ἐμπειρίας (1142a18). Mathematics is a knowing *on the way of taking-away* beings — what it *looks away from*, the concrete Dasein, it does not further regard and determine, but only the τί of πέρας, γραμμή, ἐπίπεδον. Mathematics need *not look at the concrete Dasein* to enact the ἀφαίρεσις. In σοφία, by contrast, it is *necessary* that the σοφός — or φυσικός, insofar as he is a properly-understanding one — win what he seeks *ἐξ ἐμπειρίας*. It would be a *misunderstanding* to translate ἐξ ἐμπειρίας as "from induction," as if it were the *generalization of single cases*. Rather ἐξ ἐμπειρίας is *opposed* to ἀφαίρεσις. And what is so opposed to ἀφαίρεσις is precisely the *exhibiting of the last being-fundaments of the concrete being itself*. This demands that one *make the being itself present* to see how it looks, its εἶδος, in order *from it* to draw the ἀρχή. To this belongs *acquaintance with and command of the manifold of the being*, which lets itself be appropriated only *in the course of time*. So φρόνησις is, also as regards its mode of arising, something *other* than ἐπιστήμη. (The point cuts against a facile picture of philosophy: its ἀρχαί are drawn *from experience of the being*, from long acquaintance with the concrete, not abstracted away from it — the very opposite of the mathematical χωρισμός treated in §15.)

What has been made out so far are only *preliminary* differences. The *essential* differences we win only when we recall the *guiding thread* set for distinguishing the modes of ἀληθεύειν. Aristotle oriented the regard by two respects: (1) *which* being is to be uncovered — whether the ἀεί or the ἐνδεχόμενον ἄλλως ἔχειν; (2) *how far* this being can be uncovered and safe-kept *in its ἀρχή*. Meanwhile it has become more transparent *what an ἀρχή as such is*: the ἀρχή is what already is, that from which each being properly is what it is. Characteristically, with the being that can also be otherwise, the ἀρχή — the ever-already — of φρόνησις is *anticipated in the προαίρεσις*. The question is how far the different modes of ἀληθεύειν succeed in uncovering the being in its ἀρχή and safe-keeping it, i.e. how far they grasp it in its proper being and at once hold it fast as ἕξις. This Aristotle illustrated first at ἐπιστήμη and τέχνη: τέχνη anticipates in the εἶδος the ἀρχή, the τέλος, but does not get it to grasp *in the ἔργον*; in ἐπιστήμη too no proper grasping of the ἀρχή takes place. How does it now stand with the *disclosure and safekeeping of the ἀρχή* in φρόνησις and σοφία?

#### §21. Exposition of the further task: the relation of φρόνησις and σοφία to the ἀρχαί. σοφία as νοῦς καὶ ἐπιστήμη. The task of clarifying βουλεύεσθαι as the enactment-mode of φρόνησις

We have heard that σοφία is in a certain way *ἐπιστήμη* — it makes *use* of the ἀρχαί — but is also *νοῦς*: it is νοῦς καὶ ἐπιστήμη (1141a19). It is the νοῦς that in the proper sense *aims at the ἀρχαί and uncovers them*. σοφία is *not a pure νοεῖν*: in its νοεῖν the enactment-mode of the *human* asserts itself, insofar as therein the human *speaks*; σοφία is μετὰ λόγου (VI, 6; 1140b31). Still, σοφία is no mere *διαλέγεσθαι*, but is in a certain way *νοεῖν*. The νοεῖν of νοῦς *itself* is *ἄνευ λόγου*, without speech.

How do these connections lie in φρόνησις? Can φρόνησις uncover and safe-keep the ἀρχή of the being it aims at? The analysis of the being that is φρόνησις' theme will be difficult, because *φρόνησις itself in a certain way belongs to this being* that is its own theme. For the object of φρόνησις is the πρᾶξις, the ζωή of the human, human Dasein itself; and *to the action itself belongs the deliberation, the becoming-transparent of the acting one himself*. This transparency is not a mode of regard that interestedly-detachedly contemplates the action as it *might* look. φρόνησις *belongs into the theme*; it *itself occurs* in the being it is to uncover. Thereby the difficulty of the analysis is given, and it is not easy to make the phenomenon of φρόνησις present in the right way *at one stroke*. It will show that φρόνησις *too* is νοῦς and νοεῖν, proper uncovering of the ἀρχή. But since the theme of φρόνησις, the πρᾶξις, is a being that *can be otherwise*, and accordingly its ἀρχαί too are such as can be otherwise, the comportment to this being will have a *wholly other structure* than the comportment to the ἀεί in σοφία. Insofar as both, φρόνησις and σοφία, are each *in their way* νοῦς, both are recognized by Aristotle as *βελτίστη ἕξις*. And precisely because both are so *equally ranked*, the question becomes all the harder: how far does the one have a priority over the other?

We have clarified the character of φρόνησις' ἀληθεύειν by learning that φρόνησις is *ἕξις πρακτική*: what it uncovers is from the outset addressed *in regard to its coming into question for acting*. The enactment-mode of the uncovering appropriation of the πρακτόν is *βουλεύεσθαι*, the circumspective *taking-counsel-with-oneself*. This βουλεύεσθαι is μετὰ λόγου, hence a *λογίζεσθαι*, a through-speaking. Insofar as φρόνησις' enactment-mode is βουλεύεσθαι, it must become visible *from the structure of βουλεύεσθαι* how φρόνησις gets the ἀρχαί of its theme — the ζωή of the human — into its grip. Aristotle carries the regard through by first asking: *which is the right βουλεύεσθαι? What does εὐβουλία look like?* — δεῖ δὲ λαβεῖν καὶ περὶ εὐβουλίας τί ἐστιν (VI, 10; 1142a32). At the structure of εὐβουλία, φρόνησις' enactment-mode, the character of φρόνησις *as ἀληθεύειν* first becomes visible, and precisely in respect of the *uncovering of the ἀρχή*. The second fundamental question will be: how does φρόνησις — when, like σοφία, it uncovers the ἀρχή, i.e. has the character of *νοῦς* — stand to *νοῦς itself*? From there we can understand νοῦς. Understanding νοῦς *out of* σοφία and φρόνησις is, in Heidegger's view, the *only* way to win a preliminary insight into the difficult phenomenon of νοῦς.

#### §22. εὐβουλία as the enactment-mode of φρόνησις (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 10)

The enactment-mode of φρόνησις is βουλεύεσθαι, itself a *λογίζεσθαι*, a through-speaking; so φρόνησις is a ἕξις μετὰ λόγου. But λόγος here must be grasped as *addressing-something-as-something*, λέγειν τι κατά τινος. Insofar as a being is addressed in the tendency to uncover it in the addressing, there already lies in this a *διαίρεσις*: addressing something *upon* something has *taken the addressed being apart*. All that is theme of a λόγος is, as such, a *διαιρετόν*. Whereas the being, insofar as in its nearest encountering-mode it is at first only καθόλου, given *as a whole*, is a *συγκεχυμένον*, a "poured-together." Addressing means: to *articulate* the addressed. Only on the ground of such διαίρεσις follows the *σύνθεσις* proper to λόγος: **λόγος is dihairetic-synthetic**. If now φρόνησις is to be a βελτίστη ἕξις, it must grasp the *ἀρχή* of its theme. But an ἀρχή — and all the more a last, outermost ἀρχή — is itself *no longer* something that can be addressed *as* something. The adequate addressing of an ἀρχή cannot be enacted through λόγος, insofar as λόγος is διαίρεσις. An ἀρχή can be grasped only *at itself*, not as something other; the ἀρχή is an *ἀδιαίρετον*, something whose being resists being laid apart. Accordingly there belongs to φρόνησις the possibility of a *simple grasping of the ἀρχή as such*, i.e. an uncovering-mode that *goes beyond λόγος*. Insofar as φρόνησις is a βελτίστη ἕξις, it must be *more than mere λόγος*. This corresponds exactly to the position at which we left σοφία: σοφία goes to the ἀρχαί as such, so in it something like *pure νοεῖν* is alive — for an ἀρχή, being an ἀδιαίρετον, is uncovered *not in λέγειν but in νοεῖν*. The question thus arises whether, analogously to σοφία being νοῦς καὶ ἐπιστήμη, there is in φρόνησις too the possibility, *beyond* λέγειν and λογίζεσθαι yet in connection with it, of uncovering and holding fast the ἀρχή as such — whether in it there is something like a *pure νοεῖν, a pure perceiving*.

##### a) The structure of βουλεύεσθαι

**α) Structural analysis of the action.** The regard sets out from the *making-present of the being that is uncovered in φρόνησις*. One cannot say "the being that is φρόνησις' *theme*," if by "theme" we understand the being that is object of *theoretical* regard: φρόνησις has properly *no theme*, since it does not take what it uncovers *into view as such*. The being φρόνησις uncovers is the *πρᾶξις*; therein lies human Dasein, whose ζωή is determined as ζωὴ πρακτικὴ μετὰ λόγου (*Nic. Eth.* I, 7; 1098a3).

When a determinate action is at issue, the first question is *of what* it is the action. Every action is action in relation to a determinate *of-what*. Since the ζωὴ πρακτική moves in each case in a determinate environing-world, the action is enacted *under determinate circumstances* characterizing the *situation* (*Lage*) in which Dasein finds itself. The action is marked by several moments (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 10; 1142b23): (1) that *of-which* it is the action (ὅ); (2) what must be drawn on and made ready as *means and way* to act (δι' οὗ) — to give another joy by a gift, the corresponding objects must be available; (3) these objects must be used in a determinate way (πῶς), must be in a determinate *usability* so that, oriented to what I will in the action, I can freely dispose over them; (4) every action is enacted at a determinate *time* (ὅτε); and (5) insofar as Dasein is being-with-one-another, over against *one or another* determinate human. So Dasein as respective, now-acting, is determined by its *situation* in the widest sense — and this situation is in each case *another*: circumstances, givens, times, humans change; the *sense of the action itself* changes, what I in each case will.

This whole nexus of the acting Dasein *in its respective full situation* is to be uncovered by φρόνησις. To uncover Dasein as now-acting in its full situation, in which it is to act and in which it is in each case *other*, in its *respectiveness* (*Jeweiligkeit*) — this is the accomplishment of φρόνησις. But φρόνησις is *not* a contemplation of situation and action, no taking-stock in the sense of a "disinterested" establishing, no study of the situation I am in; the moment of "interest" too does not hit φρόνησις' sense. Rather the *through-speaking itself belongs to the full action*. From the ἀρχή — from what I will, what I resolve on — up to the completed action itself, φρόνησις *belongs to the action*; at *every step* of the action φρόνησις is co-constitutive. In φρόνησις the action must be made *transparent from its ἀρχή to its τέλος*, because the action is a being that can in each case be otherwise; correspondingly φρόνησις is *co-present*, so that it *makes up* the πρᾶξις itself.

The ἀρχή of the action is the *οὗ ἕνεκα*, the for-the-sake-of-which; and this οὗ ἕνεκα is, at the action's outset, the *προαιρετόν*, what I anticipate in the *choice*: this-and-that shall now, for this-and-that human, happen from me thus-and-so. In this προαίρεσις nothing other is anticipated than *the action itself*. The ἀρχή φρόνησις has to do with is the action itself; the τέλος regarded in φρόνησις is the action itself — namely the *acted* action. Here we have with φρόνησις an *analogous relation to τέχνη*, insofar as the τεχνίτης in a way anticipates the εἶδος of the house. But the τέλος in τέχνη is *not the builder himself*; for him it is *παρά*, and *as builder* he precisely does not dispose over it — the τέλος *qua* ἔργον falls *out* of τέχνη. Whereas in φρόνησις the *action itself* is anticipated, and the τέλος of the action is itself nothing other than the action itself, to which φρόνησις belongs *as προαίρεσις*. This whole nexus from ἀρχή to τέλος is nothing other than the *full being of the action itself* — and this full being is what φρόνησις is to uncover.

Following φρόνησις' structure from its first outset: the action, as what I resolve on, is anticipated; but in the anticipation, in the ἀρχή, the *circumstances* and what belongs to *carrying out* the action are characteristically *not yet given*. Rather, precisely *out of the constant regard to what I have resolved on*, the *situation* is to become transparent. Seen from the προαιρετόν, the concrete situation of acting is still a *ζητούμενον*, something *sought*, *covered up*. (*Met.* VII, 13 characterizes the ζητούμενον as a *λανθάνον*, 1041a32: what is sought is still *concealed*.) So it is a matter of uncovering, from the regard to the action's ἀρχή, the concrete situation that is at first concealed, and thereby making the action itself transparent. This uncovering of the concealed in the sense of making-the-action-transparent is φρόνησις' affair.

But now the τέλος of the action is the action itself, and specifically the *εὐπραξία*. It is not a matter of something happening *at all*, but of the action's happening *in the right way*, so that it comes to its end *in what it can be*. Insofar as φρόνησις belongs constitutively to the πρᾶξις, φρόνησις too must in its enactment have the character of the *εὖ*. The *how* of the deliberating, λογίζεσθαι — the way on which φρόνησις uncovers the situation — is determined by the character of the action itself; and this λογίζεσθαι, the through-deliberating, is also designated *βουλεύεσθαι*, φρόνησις' enactment-mode. Accordingly βουλεύεσθαι must have the character of the εὖ; if indeed the τέλος of the πρᾶξις is the εὐπραξία, βουλεύεσθαι must be characterized by *εὐβουλία*. *As εὐβουλία, φρόνησις is properly what it is.* The question of φρόνησις' structure thus concentrates on: what is εὐβουλία, the right through-deliberating of the action from its ἀρχή to its τέλος, to the last grasping-hold?

**β) εὐβουλία as proper φρόνησις. The rightness (ὀρθότης) of εὐβουλία. The resolve (βουλή). βουλεύεσθαι as συλλογίζεσθαι. The ὀρθὸς λόγος.** This βουλεύεσθαι is no contemplation of something *present*, in the sense of a mere describing, but of something *sought*, not yet present, still to be uncovered: τὸ γὰρ βουλεύεσθαι ζητεῖν τι ἐστίν (1142a31). The character of *ζητεῖν* must be held fast from the start: the ζητεῖν moves *not* as blind trying-out but as a *being-underway* with the orientation, from the outset, (1) *from-whence*, from the ἀρχή, and (2) *toward*, to the τέλος — both only two determinations of the *one*: the πρᾶξις itself. In constant looking to the ἀρχή, the through-deliberating of the situation is a *going-toward the τέλος*. The τέλος is the action itself, as *acted, enacted*. So βουλεύεσθαι has a *direction*; it is in itself *directed toward*, such that, as it were *from the back*, the orientation is constantly toward the anticipated, the action. To βουλεύεσθαι as such belongs the structural moment of *direction*. Insofar as βουλεύεσθαι is to be directed in the right way — *εὖ* — the εὖ belongs to the enactment of βουλεύεσθαι itself. The being-directed in the right way, εὖ, is the *rightness, ὀρθότης*, of the acting, which as it were *holds through* the direction pre-sketched by the ἀρχή and τέλος of the acting: δῆλον ὅτι ὀρθότης τις ἡ εὐβουλία ἐστίν (1142b8). The worked-out rightness of the concrete action is the *ὀρθότης βουλῆς*; βουλή is the *resolve, being-resolved*: ἀλλ' ὀρθότης τίς ἐστιν ἡ εὐβουλία βουλῆς (1142b16). The working-out of the concrete situation aims at making the right *resolvedness*, as the transparency of the action, available. And insofar as this resolvedness is in fact appropriated and enacted — insofar as I *am resolved* — the action is there in its outermost possibility. The directed uncovering of the full situation *ends in the proper resolvedness toward…, in the grasping-hold itself*.

This βουλεύεσθαι, the through-deliberating, is enacted as λογίζεσθαι so that in it a *nexus of speaking* is alive, a *speaking-together*, συλλογίζεσθαι, συλλογισμός, outwardly designated "inference." Every proof-course has a *concluding-sentence*, συμπέρασμα. The concluding-sentence of βουλεύεσθαι is *the action itself*; it is not some sentence, some cognition, but *the breaking-loose of the acting one as such*. This shows how in φρόνησις the *ἔργον* lies enclosed, and how φρόνησις belongs to the being of the acting one. From this basic structure is to be understood what has constantly given interpretation difficulties: the talk of the *ὀρθὸς λόγος*. Over this concept there is "a veritable history of nonsense." From what has been said one grasps at once what is at issue: *λόγος* means *through-speaking, not "reason"*; *ὀρθός* is nothing other than the *ὀρθότης βουλῆς*, the rightness that has its structure in the peculiar mode of φρόνησις' being-directed. This being-directed rests in that, with the πρᾶξις, the λόγος belongs *to the action*; the λόγος is *ὁμολόγως τῇ ὀρέξει*. The προαίρεσις is in itself *διανοητική*, or the διάνοια in itself *προαιρετική*: *διανοητικὴ προαίρεσις* and *προαιρετικὴ διάνοια* name the same phenomenon — the *in-itself-transparent action*.

##### b) Delimitation of εὐβουλία against other modes of ἀληθεύειν: knowledge (ἐπιστήμη), sure-aim (εὐστοχία), presence-of-mind (ἀγχίνοια), view (δόξα)

Aristotle makes εὐβουλία's structure visible by *delimiting* it against other possible modes of uncovering — a method he likes. (1) Is εὐβουλία perhaps *ἐπιστήμη*, of the character of *knowing*? ἐπιστήμη μὲν δὴ οὐκ ἔστιν (οὐ γὰρ ζητοῦσι περὶ ὧν ἴσασιν, ἡ δ' εὐβουλία βουλή τις, ὁ δὲ βουλευόμενος ζητεῖ καὶ λογίζεται) (1142a34). εὐβουλία cannot be ἐπιστήμη, for to ἐπιστήμη belongs *that I know*: in knowing I have a determinate being *already uncovered there*; in ἐπιστήμη the ζητεῖν *has come to an end*; in knowing there is no *seeking* but an *already-having-found*. (2) Is εὐβουλία like *εὐστοχία*, sure-aim — the right deliberating as a property many have, that when it comes to acting they *instinctively* hit the decisive circumstances, the right moment: the security of instinct? ἀλλὰ μὴν οὐδ' εὐστοχία· ἄνευ τε γὰρ λόγου καὶ ταχύ τι ἡ εὐστοχία, βουλεύονται δὲ πολὺν χρόνον (1142b2). εὐβουλία cannot be εὐστοχία, for to εὐβουλία belongs *λόγος*, the actual through-speaking; in instinct-security I act simply, *without* proper through-speaking. Further, acting in εὐστοχία is characterized by the *ταχύ*, it happens *at one stroke*; whereas βουλεύεσθαι demands *πολὺν χρόνον* — no over-hasty acting, but the right deliberating *with time*. (3) *ἀγχίνοια* (1142b5), a νοεῖν that is *ἀγχί*, near-by something — what we render "presence of mind," the quick surveying of the situation: ἔστι δὲ εὐστοχία τις ἡ ἀγχίνοια (1142b6). ἀγχίνοια has a certain kinship with εὐστοχία, though it expresses more the *momentary*, the surveying-the-situation-at-one-stroke, while instinct-security consists more in proceeding surely in *step-by-step* pursuit. So ἀγχίνοια does not come into question as interpretation of εὐβουλία. (4) *δόξα*, view — because δόξα, being-of-a-view, in its structure *does* have a ὀρθότης: a view of something is *directed toward*; in the view I have, I mean *it is so*; in view lies, by its sense, the orientation toward the being as it shows itself to a right investigation. But: οὐδὲ δὴ δόξα ἡ εὐβουλία οὐδεμία· […] δόξης δ' ὀρθότης ἀλήθεια (1142b6). εὐβουλία can be no δόξα, for the ὀρθότης of δόξα is directed toward *ἀλήθεια*, whereas εὐβουλία is directed toward the *βουλή*, the being-resolved-toward. εὐβουλία is *not* directed toward truth or falsity, but *primarily and solely* toward being-resolved-toward. Further, δόξα is peculiarly constituted: though it has a ὀρθότης, it is *no ζητεῖν* — καὶ γὰρ ἡ δόξα οὐ ζήτησις ἀλλὰ φάσις τις ἤδη (1142b13): δόξα is no seeking; in having-a-view lies already a certain *φάσις*: I am of the view that…, I do not *seek*. δόξα does go to what can also be otherwise, to the *συγκείμενον*, and insofar it too is, like βουλεύεσθαι, a *λέγειν*, an addressing-of-something-as-something, a *διανοεῖν*, a taking-apart; being such a taking-apart λόγος, δόξα *seems* able to be true or false — but in truth it is *neither true nor false*, but *directed toward the ἀληθές*. Likewise βουλεύεσθαι can be this way or that — κακῶς or εὖ, going astray (ἁμαρτάνειν) or hitting — but the essential is that it is *directed toward*, not toward the ἀληθές but toward the βουλή, the being-resolved-toward. (This ὀρθότης is also *not* ἐπιστήμη's: ἐπιστήμη has *no* ὀρθότης at all, as it has no ἁμαρτία; it is an already-finished ἕξις, not first *underway to…*.)

Through this delimitation Aristotle has at once made εὐβουλία's phenomenon *visible*. The four possibilities against which it is bounded are *not apriori thought-up* but spring, in the through-regarding of εὐβουλία, from the *kinship of the phenomena themselves*. Still unclarified is what, within εὐβουλία, the ὀρθότης itself is.

##### c) The ὀρθότης of εὐβουλία. The thoroughgoing directedness toward the ἀγαθόν

ἐπεὶ δ' ἡ ὀρθότης πλεοναχῶς, δῆλον ὅτι οὐ πᾶσα (1142b17): there are various conceptions of ὀρθότης, but not every one hits εὐβουλία's. So the task: to determine exactly in *what sense* εὐβουλία's ὀρθότης is ὀρθότης. ὁ γὰρ ἀκρατὴς καὶ ὁ φαῦλος οὐ προτίθεται τυχεῖν ἐκ τοῦ λογισμοῦ τεύξεται, ὥστε ὀρθῶς ἔσται βεβουλευμένος, κακὸν δὲ μέγα εἰληφώς (1142b18). One driven by his passions and ill-disposed can resolve on a *κακόν*; then the ἀρχή of the action, the goal taken up in the προαίρεσις, is a κακόν and so *failed* for the whole action. Yet it is possible that, *holding fast this κακόν*, the through-speaking of the concrete situation is a *εὐλογίζεσθαι* and exactly answers to the κακόν set in the resolve; then βουλεύεσθαι is indeed *ὀρθῶς*, fully satisfying the ὀρθότης βουλῆς. Nevertheless the τέλος, the end of such deliberation — the action itself — is a *κακόν*, though at φρόνησις itself, as regards its formal enactment-mode, nothing can be faulted. But εὐβουλία's ὀρθότης is precisely to *co-constitute the ἀγαθόν* of the action. So the ὀρθότης of a βουλεύεσθαι whose τέλος is the κακόν does *not* come into question as ὀρθότης of εὐβουλία.

Conversely, it is possible that the τέλος is a genuine ἀγαθόν but the deliberating is *inadequate*, the συλλογισμός *ψευδής*: ἀλλ' ἔστιν καὶ τούτου ψευδεῖ συλλογισμῷ τυχεῖν, καὶ ὃ μὲν δεῖ ποιῆσαι τυχεῖν, δι' οὗ δὲ οὔ, ἀλλὰ ψευδῆ τὸν μέσον ὅρον εἶναι (1142b22). The συλλογισμός, or the *μέσος ὅρος*, can be ψευδής — distorting the circumstances, means and ways, not giving them as they should be in relation to the προαιρετόν. Accordingly εὐβουλία must set the τέλος as ἀγαθόν *and* be ἀγαθόν *in each of its steps*: at every step εὐβουλία must be so directed that it *has the ἀγαθόν in view* and discusses all circumstances and occasions with a view to it. Only as *ἀγαθοῦ τευκτική* does εὐβουλία's ὀρθότης come into question: ἡ γὰρ τοιαύτη ὀρθότης βουλῆς εὐβουλία, ἡ ἀγαθοῦ τευκτική (1142b21). (Time as such — whether one deliberates long or short — is no distinguishing character; what matters above all is that the *time of the action itself* be an ἀγαθόν.) Insofar as εὐβουλία's ὀρθότης is in every step ἀγαθοῦ τευκτική, it is ὀρθότης ἡ κατὰ τὸ ὠφέλιμον, καὶ οὗ δεῖ καὶ ὡς καὶ ὅτε (1142b27) — the rightness in regard to what comes into question for carrying out the προαιρετὸν ἀγαθόν, determined as (1) *οὗ δεῖ*, (2) *ὡς*, (3) *ὅτε*: *what* is needed, *how* it is used, and *when*. All these moments must have the character of the ἀγαθόν. Further: ἔτι ἔστιν καὶ ἁπλῶς εὖ βεβουλεῦσθαι καὶ πρός τι τέλος (1142b28): εὐβουλία can be enacted either as a through-speaking related to the *ἀγαθόν simply*, or as one that is *πρός τι τέλος*, related to a determinate τέλος that is again πρός τι, related to another.

Aristotle finally determines εὐβουλία: ὃ δὴ τῶν φρονίμων τὸ εὖ βεβουλεῦσθαι, ἡ εὐβουλία εἴη ἂν ὀρθότης ἡ κατὰ τὸ συμφέρον πρὸς τὸ τέλος, οὗ ἡ φρόνησις ἀληθὴς ὑπόληψίς ἐστιν (1142b31): εὐβουλία is the rightness in regard to what is *contributory for the end*, for the right bringing-to-end of an action. The τέλος itself is in its turn *grasped in advance* in φρόνησις: φρόνησις is *ὑπόληψις ἀληθὴς τοῦ τέλους*. ὑπόληψις belongs to ὑπολαμβάνειν, *to anticipate*. (The *ὑπό* recurs in fundamental concepts: ὑποκείμενον, in Latin *substantia*; ὑπομένον, what always already remains-there; ὑπάρχον, what is in advance already there so that it *rules* — ὑπάρχειν is used of the being of the ἀρχή.) φρόνησις is ὑπόληψις ἀληθὴς τοῦ τέλους, "what grasps the τέλος *in advance*," so that this τέλος *ὑπό*, before all, is already there. And εὐβουλία, insofar as it is ὀρθότης ἡ κατὰ τὸ συμφέρον πρὸς τὸ τέλος, is nothing other than the *enactment-mode of concrete φρόνησις*.

φρόνησις itself, insofar as it is a constitutive moment of the πρᾶξις, refers expressly to a being that *can also be otherwise*. All that is possible object of an action belongs to the being that has the character of *respectiveness* (*Jeweiligkeit*), and specifically in the sense of the *ἔσχατον*. The πρακτόν is ultimately an *ἔσχατον*. We must understand more exactly what this means: φρόνησις must be *familiar with the ἔσχατα* — and it will show that these are the *affair of νοῦς*.

#### §23. φρόνησις and νοῦς (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 12)

##### a) νοῦς in σοφία and φρόνησις. The double direction of νοῦς: σοφία: νοῦς → πρῶτα; φρόνησις: νοῦς → ἔσχατα. The practical syllogism. Practical νοῦς as αἴσθησις

ἔστιν δὲ τῶν καθ' ἕκαστα καὶ τῶν ἐσχάτων ἅπαντα τὰ πρακτά· καὶ γὰρ τὸν φρόνιμον δεῖ γινώσκειν αὐτά (1143a32). *ἔσχατον* says literally the outermost limit — here, the outermost limit of the *λογίζεσθαι*, that at which the through-speaking comes to an end, where it as it were *stands still*. Aristotle illustrates the ἔσχατον in *Met.* VII, 7, describing the physician's διανοεῖν: γίγνεται δὴ τὸ ὑγιὲς νοήσαντος οὕτως· ἐπειδὴ τοδὶ ὑγίεια, ἀνάγκη, εἰ ὑγιὲς ἔσται, τοδὶ ὑπάρξαι […] καὶ οὕτως ἀεὶ νοεῖ, ἕως ἂν ἀγάγῃ εἰς τοῦτο ὃ αὐτὸς δύναται ἔσχατον ποιεῖν (1032b6): since such-and-such is the healthy state, then, if health is to be, such-and-such must be present in advance; and so he keeps deliberating until he has led the deliberation and himself to *what he can himself do as the outermost* — to that at which he can *step into the treatment*. The ἔσχατον is the being-moment at the concrete being where the physician's *intervention sets in*, and conversely that at which the deliberating *comes to a standstill*. The ἔσχατον is the outermost limit of deliberating, and so the *making-present of the state of affairs at which the action sets in*.

Now, Aristotle designates the πρακτά too as *ἔσχατα*. The question arises how these ἔσχατα are grasped in φρόνησις' deliberation. How far does φρόνησις, as a λογίζεσθαι, contain a grasping of the being that *goes beyond λόγος*? How far does φρόνησις contain *νοῦς*, a νοεῖν? Aristotle lifts this out by comparison with σοφία: καὶ ὁ νοῦς τῶν ἐσχάτων ἐπ' ἀμφότερα· καὶ γὰρ τῶν πρώτων ὅρων καὶ τῶν ἐσχάτων νοῦς ἐστι καὶ οὐ λόγος (1143a35). The simple *meaning-of* the ἔσχατα is possible *toward two sides*; νοῦς can grasp an outermost in a *double direction* — νοῦς relates both to the *πρῶτοι ὅροι*, the first delimitations, the ἀρχαί simply, the last elements of what always is, *and* to the outermost in the sense of the *respective single this-here*. Of both there is *no longer a discussing* but only still a *νοεῖν*.

Aristotle determines the two possibilities: καὶ ὁ μὲν κατὰ τὰς ἀποδείξεις τῶν ἀκινήτων ὅρων καὶ πρώτων, ὁ δ' ἐν ταῖς πρακτικαῖς τοῦ ἐσχάτου καὶ ἐνδεχομένου καὶ τῆς ἑτέρας προτάσεως (1143b1). In the first, νοεῖν concerns the last exits of the *ἀπόδειξις*, the theoretical proving of the ἀκίνητα, the being not in movement — nothing other than the ἀρχαί that are σοφία's object. The other is the *counter-direction* of this νοεῖν: within the *practical* (the text has ἐν ταῖς πρακτικαῖς [ἀποδείξεσιν]; Victorius reads ἐν τοῖς πρακτικοῖς [λόγοις]) there is also a νοεῖν, and here the νοεῖν goes to the *ἔσχατον*. ἔσχατον is the counter-concept to what in ἀπόδειξις was the πρῶτον; to the ἀκίνητον, the ἀεί, corresponds the ἐνδεχόμενον. The simple grasping in νοεῖν here relates to an *ἔσχατον that is in each case another*.

And it relates, as Aristotle says, to the *other premise*, ἑτέρα πρότασις (1143b3). πρότασις, premise, is here broadly taken as what is *set-in-advance*, what stands before the concluding sentence. Such προτάσεις occur not only in the ἀποδείξεις of the ἐπιστῆμαι; in public rhetoric, e.g., the προτάσεις are the *ἔνδοξα*, opinions that stand in repute. What matters: in our connection both the proof in the sense of the ἐπιστῆμαι *and* the λογίζεσθαι in the sense of circumspective through-speaking have the structure of the *συλλογισμός*. βουλεύεσθαι is structurally set into a *συλλογισμός* — the "practical syllogism." A φρόνησις sets in with a *προαίρεσις*: for the sake of an ἀγαθόν — whatever it be — this shall be acted (*first premise*). Now the circumstances and the situation of the action are so-and-so (*second premise*). Therefore I act thus-and-so (*conclusion*). In the first premise it is a matter of grasping the οὗ ἕνεκα, which is an ἐνδεχόμενον; in the second, of finding the *ἔσχατον*, the outermost at which the λογίζεσθαι halts. And now Aristotle says: τούτων οὖν ἔχειν δεῖ αἴσθησιν, αὕτη δ' ἐστὶ νοῦς (1143b5) — "it is needed for this that one *have αἴσθησις*, simple perceiving." In deliberating the situation in which I am to act, I finally strike on the *simple grasping* of determinate present states of affairs, determinate circumstances, a determinate time. All deliberating *ends in an αἴσθησις*. This perceiving-simply within φρόνησις *is νοῦς*.

##### b) Practical νοῦς and αἴσθησις (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 9; III, 5). αἴσθησις as grasping the ἔσχατα. Comparison with ἀνάλυσις in geometry. Geometrical and practical αἴσθησις

ὁ μὲν γὰρ νοῦς τῶν ὅρων, ὧν οὐκ ἔστιν λόγος, ἡ δὲ τοῦ ἐσχάτου, οὗ οὐκ ἔστιν ἐπιστήμη ἀλλ' αἴσθησις, οὐχ ἡ τῶν ἰδίων, ἀλλ' οἵᾳ αἰσθανόμεθα ὅτι τὸ ἐν τοῖς μαθηματικοῖς ἔσχατον τρίγωνον· στήσεται γὰρ κἀκεῖ (1142a25). In φρόνησις the states of affairs are grasped *purely as they show themselves*; such grasping is the affair of αἴσθησις. But this perceiving does *not* relate to the *specific* objects of perceiving in the narrowest sense, the *ἴδια* of αἴσθησις. (*De Anima* II, 6 laid out the ἴδια αἰσθητά: λέγω δ' ἴδιον μὲν ὃ μὴ ἐνδέχεται ἑτέρᾳ αἰσθήσει αἰσθάνεσθαι καὶ περὶ ὃ μὴ ἐνδέχεται ἀπατηθῆναι, 418a11 — the ἴδια are the respective objects for seeing, hearing, smelling: the ἴδιον for seeing is color, for hearing the tone; these ἴδια are for their αἰσθήσεις *ἀεὶ ἀληθῆ*, always true. From them Aristotle distinguishes the *κοινὰ αἰσθητά*, κοινὰ πάσαις, objects common to all the senses, like σχῆμα and μέγεθος.) What concerns φρόνησις and the simple grasping of the ἔσχατον at which πρᾶξις intervenes is *not* such an αἴσθησις of the ἴδια, but an αἴσθησις in the *widest* sense of the word, as it is ordinarily given in daily Dasein: in αἴσθησις I see the *whole* of states of affairs — the whole of street, houses, trees, humans — such that this αἴσθησις has the character of *simple establishing*.

It is such an αἴσθησις by whose help we perceive ὅτι τὸ ἐν τοῖς μαθηματικοῖς ἔσχατον τρίγωνον (1142a28) — such an αἴσθησις as plays a fundamental role in *geometry*, where it grasps the ἔσχατον of geometry: the *τρίγωνον*, triangle. Note that in Greek geometry the triangle is the last, most elementary plane figure, arising from the polygons through a *διαγράφειν*, "writing-through": the polygons are through-spoken by διαγράφειν until they are taken apart into nothing but triangles, so that the triangles are the *ἔσχατα* at which the διαιρεῖν comes to a stand. In the αἴσθησις that occurs in geometry, I see the triangle *at one stroke* as the most originary element, itself no longer resolvable into more elementary figures. As in geometry an αἰσθάνεσθαι gives the ἔσχατον, so too in φρόνησις. Essential is that in this αἴσθησις something shows itself *simply, absolutely*. Aristotle stresses that in this way of coming-to-an-end of the regard, the deliberating *στήσεται* (1142a29), "stands still"; here it goes no further. This αἴσθησις — here in φρόνησις as in geometry — is a *coming-to-a-stand* in which it is only and essentially a matter of *bringing oneself into position* over against a matter, *letting it simply be encountered*. In such νοεῖν it is a matter of a *simple making-present of the matter itself*, so that it speaks *purely from itself* and no longer needs a discussing, a pointing-out *from our side*. Here one can still say: *φαίνεται*, the matter *shows itself*. The sole possibility is *to look toward* and, in looking, to grasp.

Aristotle describes this connection far more fully at *Nic. Eth.* III, 5 (1112b11), returning to the geometrical state of affairs, the *διάγραμμα*. He sets out from deliberating: one does *not* deliberate over the *τέλος* — the τέλος is object of the *resolve*. Object of deliberating is the *συμφέρον πρὸς τὸ τέλος*, what comes into question for the right bringing-to-end of what is resolved. βουλευόμεθα δ' οὐ περὶ τῶν τελῶν ἀλλὰ περὶ τῶν πρὸς τὰ τέλη· οὔτε γὰρ ἰατρὸς βουλεύεται εἰ ὑγιάσει, οὔτε ῥήτωρ εἰ πείσει, οὔτε πολιτικὸς εἰ εὐνομίαν ποιήσει, οὐδὲ τῶν λοιπῶν οὐδεὶς περὶ τοῦ τέλους (1112b11). The physician does not deliberate *whether* he should heal — that lies in the sense of his existence itself, for that he has resolved *as* physician; just as little does the rhetor deliberate whether he should convince. ἀλλὰ θέμενοι τέλος τι πῶς καὶ διὰ τίνων ἔσται σκοποῦσιν (1112b15): the τέλος is a *τέλος τεθέν*, an end *set and made-fast*. On this they do *not* look in their deliberating; what they look on is the *πῶς καὶ διὰ τίνων*, the how and through-which-means-and-ways. And they look around in the concrete situation of their acting until — ἕως ἂν ἔλθωσιν ἐπὶ τὸ πρῶτον αἴτιον, ὃ ἐν τῇ εὑρέσει ἔσχατόν ἐστιν (1112b18) — they strike, in the through-regarding, on the *first αἴτιον* from which they can intervene, which in the *finding* of the whole states of affairs is the *outermost* of the deliberation. ὁ γὰρ βουλευόμενος ἔοικεν ζητεῖν καὶ ἀναλύειν τὸν εἰρημένον τρόπον ὥσπερ διάγραμμα […], καὶ τὸ ἔσχατον ἐν τῇ ἀναλύσει πρῶτον εἶναι ἐν τῇ γενέσει (1112b20): the deliberating one seeks and *analyzes* in the said manner, as with a geometrical figure; and the *ἔσχατον of the ἀνάλυσις* is the *first* at which the ποίησις, the proper becoming, sets in. This passage matters because here Aristotle speaks *not* of ποίησις but expressly of *πρᾶξις* in the narrower sense.

This αἴσθησις, at which the deliberating comes to a standstill, is a *distinguished* one. It differs from the αἴσθησις in mathematics: ἀλλ' αὕτη μᾶλλον αἴσθησις ἢ φρόνησις, ἐκείνης δὲ ἄλλο εἶδος (1142a29). The geometrical αἴσθησις in which I see the last figure-element, the triangle, is *μᾶλλον αἴσθησις*, more pure perceiving, pure grasping, than the αἴσθησις of φρόνησις — for in geometry it is a matter *only* of the pure contemplative establishing. The αἴσθησις of φρόνησις has *another look*: for φρόνησις is, by its sense, *also in this αἴσθησις still πρακτική*. The αἴσθησις of φρόνησις is, *as φρόνησις*, related to the πρακτά. It is indeed a *last looking* on the states of affairs, but this looking is in φρόνησις *no mere looking*, but a *circumspective looking* — led by the ὀρθότης, directed toward the τέλος, the εὐπραξία — so that the objects grasped in it have the character of the *συμφέρον*.

##### c) φρόνησις and σοφία as mutually opposed highest modes of ἀληθεύειν (= νοῦς). ἀεί and moment-of-vision (Augenblick). Outlook: νοῦς and διαλέγεσθαι. Aristotle and Plato

φρόνησις has become visible in the fundamental structural moment that in it too something like a *pure perceiving* is enacted, one *no longer* falling in the domain of λόγος. Insofar as this pure perceiving goes to the *ἔσχατον*, it is αἴσθησις; but insofar as this αἴσθησις does *not* go to the ἴδια, and is nonetheless a simple perceiving, it is *νοῦς*. Therefore Aristotle can say: ἀντίκειται μὲν δὴ τῷ νῷ (1142a25) — φρόνησις *lies opposite* νοῦς, if νοῦς is understood as the νοῦς in σοφία that aims at the ἀρχαί. φρόνησις is *structurally the same* as σοφία: it is an ἀληθεύειν *ἄνευ λόγου* — that is the common of φρόνησις and σοφία. But the pure grasping lies, with φρόνησις, on the *opposite side*. We have here *two possibilities of νοῦς*: νoῦς in the outermost concretion, and νοῦς in the outermost καθόλου, in the most general generality. The νοῦς of φρόνησις aims at the outermost in the sense of the *ἔσχατον simply*.

φρόνησις is the *catching-sight of the this-time*, of the concrete this-timeness of the *momentary situation*. As αἴσθησις it is the *glance of the eye* — the *Augenblick*, the moment-of-vision — upon the respective concrete, which as such *can always be otherwise*. Whereas the νοεῖν in σοφία is the regarding of what is *ἀεί*, what is always present *in selfsameness*. **Time — the moment-of-vision and the always-being — functions here as the *discrimen* of the νοεῖν in φρόνησις and σοφία.** So it has become clear: both φρόνησις and σοφία, on the ground that they *bear νοεῖν in themselves*, are possibilities in which the being, according to the basic modes of its being, is disclosed and graspable *ἐπ' ἀμφότερα* (1143a35), "toward both sides," down into its ἀρχαί ultimately. On the ground of this being-related to the ἀρχαί, φρόνησις and σοφία are the *highest possibilities of disclosing the being itself*. Insofar as they are modes of Dasein, they make up its *being-mode*: σοφία being the *being-positioned toward the being of the world in the full sense*, φρόνησις being the *being-positioned toward the being as one's own Dasein*. But with this the very question poses itself: *what is the sense of being that gives the guiding thread on the ground of which Aristotle comes to award σοφία the priority over φρόνησις?*

*[Heidegger notes in the manuscript that six sessions had meanwhile been cancelled; he therefore resumes here with a reflection on the sense of the Aristotle-part.]* We have here made clear to ourselves the phenomenon of ἀληθεύειν as a possibility of human Dasein, which is in its being determined thereby. The aim of this regard was to *prepare us for the interpretation of a Platonic dialogue*, to put us in the bearing to *co-enact, step by step, and really grasp* the deliberating as it is carried out in such a dialogue. Only if we win this bearing do we have the guarantee of *seeing the matters* spoken of. A dialogue is enacted in *διαλέγεσθαι*. We will learn more exactly how this διαλέγεσθαι, seen from the maturity of Aristotle's philosophical regard, turns out to be a *justified preliminary stage of philosophizing*. To show this, we must already be borne further, onto a *higher stage of philosophizing*, in order from there to understand the "dialogue" *retrospectively*. Already from this expression, διαλέγεσθαι, one sees that it is a matter of *λόγος*. We will close our regard of ἀληθεύειν by bringing the *highest and last stage of ἀληθεύειν* into connection with the question of the *reach and accomplishment-mode of λόγος* within a theoretical regard.

This is the hinge of the whole Introductory Part. φρόνησις and σoφία have been shown to be structurally identical (both ἀληθεύειν ἄνευ λόγου, both bearing νοῦς) yet *oppositely directed* — and the axis of their opposition is *time itself*: the Augenblick against the ἀεί. Heidegger has thereby prepared two things at once. He has won, from Aristotle, the phenomenon of the *moment-of-vision* as the disclosive glance upon the concrete situation — the direct ancestor of the *Augenblick* in *Being and Time* §68. And he has posed the question that the Plato interpretation must answer: since διαλέγεσθαι is a matter of *λόγος*, and λόγος has now been shown to be *derivative* over against the pure νοεῖν in which alone the ἀρχαί and ἔσχατα are grasped, Plato's dialectic can be only a *preliminary stage* — justified, but to be understood from a higher standpoint. The priority of σοφία over φρόνησις, decided in §24, will rest entirely on the Greek sense of being as *constant presence*, against which the moment-of-vision, for all its disclosive power, discloses only a being that can be otherwise.

#### §24. The decision of the priority question between φρόνησις and σοφία in favor of σοφία (*Nic. Eth.* VI, 13)

##### a) The difficulty of the decision: advantages and defects in φρόνησις and σοφία. The question of the relation to human Dasein. Self-standingness and un-self-standingness of ἀληθεύειν
